  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5885185c-03db-42be-aedb-0ae52b8a2eaa'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2374551398630851359">A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.<br/><br/>When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during a terrible storm, Emily’s life changes forever.   <span id="freeText2374551398630851359" style="display:none">A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.<br /><br />When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during a terrible storm, Emily’s life changes forever. Suddenly allied with a winged horse she’d always thought was mythical, Emily is thrust into the center of a fierce battle between the Roman gods and a terrifying race of multiarmed stone warriors called the Nirads. Emily must team up with a thief named Paelen, the goddess Diana, and a boy named Joel in order to return Pegasus to Olympus and rescue the gods from a certain death.<br /><br /> Along the way, Emily and her companions will fight monsters, run from a government agency that is prepared to dissect Pegasus, and even fly above the Manhattan skyline—all as part of a quest to save Olympus before time runs out.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6187574-jessika-beaty"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1550024694i/6187574._UY100_CR6,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6187574-jessika-beaty">Jessika Beaty  </a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I actually don't think it's that violent for adults, maybe for little kids. There is a lot of shooting going on especially with the main characters th<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I actually don't think it's that violent for adults, maybe for little kids. There is a lot of shooting going on especially with the main characters the author loves to do. It's brutal in my opinion. While Harry Potter definitely is more violent with the killings, I honestly think that Flame of Olympus is worse. Just using guns on the main characters, a lot of torture scenes from the CIA, some of the CIA agents wanted to attack children while the Olympian Gods were at a grocery store and they had to beg the agents to let the kids go free and let everyone else go free. It's just be cautious. :) My humble opinion. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3119201814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2817390693407163791">I've wanted to read a story with Pegasus present for ages now and my hubby bought me this one for Christmas - it was on my wishlist. It didn't take me long to pick it up and I had it finished within 1,5 days. This was such a fun and fast paced read and I'm glad I can share this book and review with you guys!<br/><br/><a href='https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/about-the-book.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947475._SX540_.jpg' alt='' width='669' height='148' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><p>
  
    <strong>A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.</strong>
  
</p><br/><p>
  
    <strong>When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during </strong></p></span>
  <span id="freeText2817390693407163791" style="display:none">I've wanted to read a story with Pegasus present for ages now and my hubby bought me this one for Christmas - it was on my wishlist. It didn't take me long to pick it up and I had it finished within 1,5 days. This was such a fun and fast paced read and I'm glad I can share this book and review with you guys!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/about-the-book.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947475._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="669" height="148" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><p>
  
    <strong>A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.</strong>
  
</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during a terrible storm, Emily’s life changes forever. Suddenly allied with a winged horse she’d always thought was mythical, Emily is thrust into the center of a fierce battle between the Roman gods and a terrifying race of multiarmed stone warriors called the Nirads. Emily must team up with a thief named Paelen, the goddess Diana, and a boy named Joel in order to return Pegasus to Olympus and rescue the gods from a certain death.</strong>
  
</p><br><p>
  
    <strong>Along the way, Emily and her companions will fight monsters, run from a government agency that is prepared to dissect Pegasus, and even fly above the Manhattan skyline—all as part of a quest to save Olympus before time runs out.</strong>
  
</p><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/my-thoughts-1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947476._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="669" height="148" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>We follow two main characters; <strong>Emily</strong> (a human girl) and <strong>Paelen</strong> (an Olympian thief). Both were truly fun to read about seeing they were completely different characters. I love how strong minded Emily is, and how she went above and beyond to keep Pegasus safe and how she tries to keep the Nyriads from destroying the world.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <p>
    
      <strong>
        <i>"It's really you isn't it?" Emily whispered softly as she stroked the soft muzzle. "You're Pegasus, aren't you?" The stallion...nudged her hand, inviting another stroke. In that one rain-drenched instant, Emily felt her world changing. Forever.</i>
      </strong>
    
  </p>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>Paelen was quite interesting because at first he isn't your typical good guy, he's quiet selfish really. which isn't a particular attractive trait haha, but still I liked him. He was quite the character and quite funny from time to time. And through Paelen we learn so much more about Olympus along the way, which was something I was really curious about beforehand so I gobbled everything up so fast and truly couldn't get enough of it.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <p>
    <em>
      
        <strong>"He flies because he has wings.<br>I would have thought even you could figure that out for yourself."</strong>
      
    </em>
    <br>
    <em>
      
        <strong>- Paelen</strong>
      
    </em>
  </p>
  <br>
</blockquote><br><strong>Pegasus</strong> was the main reason why I wanted to read this book in the first place because helloooo: who doesn't think Pegasus is awesome?! Well, I do anyway haha. And I was not disappointed by his presence. I think the author did a great job at portraying this majestic creature the way she did. On his own, he was a truly interesting 'character' and then there's also the forming bond/friendship with Emily that's developing throughout the book, which was nicely written down.<br><br>I Truly cannot wait to see what more adventures these two are going to experience - thankfully book 2 and 3 are on its way as we speak, so I'm able to continue their story very soon!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/conclusion.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947477.jpg" alt="" width="280" height="96" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So yeah, conclusion... It's been a while since I've last read a Middle Grade book and I was thoroughly surprised by how entertaining The Flame of Olympus turned out to be. Sure, in all honesty (I'm always honest btw, but you know... it's just a phrase haha): you just can't expect the story to have as much depth compared to most YA and adult fantasy book you know? Keep in mind it's written as a middle grade book and when I look at it that way (the only way you should really look at it, because it IS a middle grade book) I'm definitely of an opinion that it has quite some depth present, which I wasn't expecting to be honest. It's just a really great first book in this new to me series and I'm so excited to find out what more adventures there'll come for Pegasus and his friends and how the entirety of the series will grow as well, with each new installment that follows after this one.<br><br>I'd <b>definitely (and highly) recommend</b> this one to anyone who likes a fantasy/Roman mythology inspired story that'll sweep you off your feet (almost quite literally even, thanks to Pegasus ;)). An enchanting, thrilling and entertaining, action packed read is guaranteed when you pick up this book, whether you're 9 years old or 90 years old!<br> 
  
    <strong>"A winning mix of modern adventure and classic fantasy."</strong>
  
  <br>
  
    <strong>- Rick Riordan</strong>
  
 <br>Thanks for reading!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/melissa-orange.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560676524i/27676428._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="590" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_387095969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/387095969" />
    <a title="Wonderlandreviews30" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2721647-wonderlandreviews30"><img alt="Wonderlandreviews30" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380054294p2/2721647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/387095969?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wonderlandreviews30" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wonderlandreviews30" href="/user/show/2721647-wonderlandreviews30">Wonderlandreviews30</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387095969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16684719668114431489">Searching my way through the Barnes and noble book shelves, I didn't expect to find Pegasus: The flame of Olympus. I was intrigued by the beautiful cover art and what I read from the inside flap. Another thing that caught my attention was the praise from bestseller Rick Rick Riordian. Now I never been fond of authors giving praises to another author, but for some reason I trusted Rick Riordian's praise because I am such a huge fan of his books series and I love Greek and Roman mythology.<br/><br/> Now str</span>
  <span id="freeText16684719668114431489" style="display:none">Searching my way through the Barnes and noble book shelves, I didn't expect to find Pegasus: The flame of Olympus. I was intrigued by the beautiful cover art and what I read from the inside flap. Another thing that caught my attention was the praise from bestseller Rick Rick Riordian. Now I never been fond of authors giving praises to another author, but for some reason I trusted Rick Riordian's praise because I am such a huge fan of his books series and I love Greek and Roman mythology.<br /><br /> Now straight to the book review! I can't express how much I enjoyed this book. Pegasus: the flame of Olympus focuses on two main characters, Emily and Paelen. I loved Emily from start to finish. Emily was a go getter type of girl. She spoke her mind and even through a broken leg Emily wanted to fight! Emily did what she had to do to save Pegasus and keep the Nirads from destroying the world. Now, Paelen I didn't care for at the beginning. Paelen was selfish and only thought of his own needs. But as I kept reading, Paelen started to grow on me. Paelen realized his faults and what wrong he did. He also made me laugh a few times as he was being interrogated by Agent J. I also loved Emily's friend Joel but I won't go too much into him.<br /><br />I will not discuss the plot because I want people to read this book! All I will say is not once was I disappointed and when the book ended, my heart fell out of my chest. I didn't want this great adventure that I got locked into to end. I will gladly say there will be two more books coming out and I can't wait!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16684719668114431489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_401927117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401927117" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2513302-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378669583p2/2513302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/401927117?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/2513302-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442444096" href="/book/show/12541481-the-flame-of-olympus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401927117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17510402782945076177">I was really excited about this book. Like, really excited. But as I am beginning to realize, Pegasus (or unicorns, as the case may be) does not guarantee a good book. (As a side note, I once was really excited for a book about killer unicorns that turned out to be really lame.)<br/>This book totally killed its potential, let’s see, right about the time I read the sentence starting with a dependent clause. Eye twitch. No, actually, I kinda lost interest with the prologue. Like Ranger’s Apprentice, th</span>
  <span id="freeText17510402782945076177" style="display:none">I was really excited about this book. Like, really excited. But as I am beginning to realize, Pegasus (or unicorns, as the case may be) does not guarantee a good book. (As a side note, I once was really excited for a book about killer unicorns that turned out to be really lame.)<br />This book totally killed its potential, let’s see, right about the time I read the sentence starting with a dependent clause. Eye twitch. No, actually, I kinda lost interest with the prologue. Like Ranger’s Apprentice, this one tried to start out all badass and stuff, like, “Oh no, there’s war in Olympus and the gods simply can’t win on their own!” Which sometimes happens, even to gods...except this time, the focus was on some nobody who wanted to steal Pegasus in the midst of the fighting. These things also happen, but, uh, there’s already a perfectly good thief/trickster god in the Roman pantheon, name of Mercury, and, oh shit, it seems that the author has conveniently killed him off so people like me can’t put up their hands and say, “But, but...” Already annoyed by that.<br />Then, and I quote, “Somehow” the gods are capable not only of being wounded, but dying as well, while their enemies are conveniently untouchable—except for this one time when Diana uses her dead brother’s spear to wound one of them, but that was just a fluke, ya’ll. I HATE “somehow” explanations. The gods can die. Fine, that’s shaking things up a little. But don’t put me off with “somehows,” because that’s just the author’s excuse for not figuring her shit out ahead of time. “Somehow the gods are dying. Not sure how yet, but I’ll figure it out eventually. Don’t worry your pretty little head, Reader.”<br />In fact, there are so many “somehows” in this book that by the time I was 100 pages in, I was no longer entirely sure that the author knew what her characters were doing AT ALL. “Somehow” the main character knows what Pegasus is thinking. Well, great. How? Mind meld? The eyes are the windows of the soul? Pegasus can project his thoughts? No, it’s “somehow” again.<br />So I said “somehow” I’ll just have to live on without knowing how this book ends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17510402782945076177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_579830242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579830242" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8443587-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340608340p2/8443587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579830242?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/8443587-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8443587-amy?shelf=kids-book">kids-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579830242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14087838768704156675">Okay...this is a children's book. It is for people 8 and up. It is not complex. It is not deep. It is not adult fiction. It isn't even YA fiction. It is not as complicated nor as deep as Harry Potter or Percy Jackson. It is perfect for the 3rd, 4th, 5th, 6th grade set. <br/><br/>With that being said, I am an adult and I read it after my 9 year old daughter. I wanted to see what was in it. I don't read many of her books but this one held my attention and I wanted to know what happened. I will read the next</span>
  <span id="freeText14087838768704156675" style="display:none">Okay...this is a children's book. It is for people 8 and up. It is not complex. It is not deep. It is not adult fiction. It isn't even YA fiction. It is not as complicated nor as deep as Harry Potter or Percy Jackson. It is perfect for the 3rd, 4th, 5th, 6th grade set. <br /><br />With that being said, I am an adult and I read it after my 9 year old daughter. I wanted to see what was in it. I don't read many of her books but this one held my attention and I wanted to know what happened. I will read the next three books (not yet released in US...I am awaiting a set from UK Ebay) and my daughter can't wait to get them. <br /><br />I can see where as an adult I could find fault with some of the characters, some of the bad guys and some of the conclusions. (Neil Gaiman Neverwhere is a little more MY style and so is The Veil of Gold by Kim Wilkins.) Remember it is children's literature and is listed as 8 and up. <br /><br />If you have a young daughter/child who isn't ready for Percy (like Harry Potter, Percy increases in difficulty and situation) she will love this book. Boys will enjoy it too if they are not hung up on the female lead. She has a male side-kick and another main character, Paelen, is male. <br /><br />It is a great introduction into the Roman Gods. The lead of Pegasus is wonderful. I will be interested to see how if there is any difference in the US published version from the UK version. (I do have to admit...the publisher needs a better proof-reader!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14087838768704156675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_269474768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269474768" />
    <a title="skippity_doo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7520066-skippity-doo"><img alt="skippity_doo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360502238p2/7520066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269474768?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="skippity_doo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="skippity_doo" href="/user/show/7520066-skippity-doo">skippity_doo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer269474768&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269474768" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17159761123069999156">Overall, I felt a bit frustrated by this book. I really wanted to LOVE it, and while I did enjoy it in parts, I kept feeling like it needed MORE. Even by the end I couldn't quite work out quite what age it was supposed to be pitched at - the language was a little juvenile for it to be YA, but the premise, the age of the protagonist and the interrogation/torture scenes, whilst not being overly grim, made me feel like it was a little old for 9-12s.<br/><br/>I couldn't really get a handle on the writing styl</span>
  <span id="freeText17159761123069999156" style="display:none">Overall, I felt a bit frustrated by this book. I really wanted to LOVE it, and while I did enjoy it in parts, I kept feeling like it needed MORE. Even by the end I couldn't quite work out quite what age it was supposed to be pitched at - the language was a little juvenile for it to be YA, but the premise, the age of the protagonist and the interrogation/torture scenes, whilst not being overly grim, made me feel like it was a little old for 9-12s.<br /><br />I couldn't really get a handle on the writing style at first - the prologue had me wincing all the way through - but as the plot started to grab me I began to notice it less. (Or, perhaps, it got smoother - I'm not entirely sure.)I also found some of the dialogue a little wordy - not Diana, who would use a more formal register, but once or twice Joel's speech jumped out at me. I also found the "Pegs" nickname extremely irritating, but I can see a 13-year-old coming up with a nickname along those lines, so I tried to let it slide. I found the ending a little problematic in that Emily's "rebirth" healed her leg injury - I was thinking that a protagonist with war wounds pitched to young girls was a really interesting choice, but then we hit the reset button. <br /><br />The main character, Emily, was sweet and likeable enough and seemed to have a good, sensible head on her shoulders (going to fetch Joel for help, suggesting the glue instead of stitching, and executing the hair dye disguise, etc.) The plot moved at a good pace, despite being utterly predictable, but I enjoyed the small detours around New York City, like the carriage horses scene. I enjoyed the way in which the characters began to slowly form a team, and start to trust one another. I felt like the setup was good, but would have preferred a little more time on Mount Olympus - the ending felt a bit rushed.<br /><br />In conclusion, I wish the author had a smoother style and had been brave enough to go off the beaten path in terms of the setup/conflict/resolutions which happened. I will probably read the sequels anyway, and hope for the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17159761123069999156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_347283096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347283096" />
    <a title="Liviania" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania"><img alt="Liviania" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218840926p2/1430644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/347283096?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviania" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviania" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania">Liviania</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442444096" href="/book/show/12541481-the-flame-of-olympus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347283096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6541101481242598794">Percy Jackson fans will be happy to learn that there's a new set of Olympians in town. Originally published in the UK, Kate O'Hearn's Pegasus trilogy is coming to the US. Released just last month was the first book, THE FLAME OF OLYMPUS.<br/><br/>Written in the third point of view, the narration flips back and forth between Paelen, a thief god, and Emily, a young New Yorker. Paelen attempted to steal Pegasus' bridle during a battle between the Olympians and Nirads and ended up zapped to present time. Emil</span>
  <span id="freeText6541101481242598794" style="display:none">Percy Jackson fans will be happy to learn that there's a new set of Olympians in town. Originally published in the UK, Kate O'Hearn's Pegasus trilogy is coming to the US. Released just last month was the first book, THE FLAME OF OLYMPUS.<br /><br />Written in the third point of view, the narration flips back and forth between Paelen, a thief god, and Emily, a young New Yorker. Paelen attempted to steal Pegasus' bridle during a battle between the Olympians and Nirads and ended up zapped to present time. Emily found Pegasus injured on her roof and a group of men in black found Paelen with the bridle. But both Pegasus and the bridle are needed to save Olympus.<br /><br />No adventure is complete if the ragtag band of heroes isn't likeable. Emily and her classmate Joel are resourceful children willing to work hard to protect their friends. Joel may need to learn to control his temper, but Emily is already skilled at doing the right thing even when its hard. Paelen could take a few lessons from her. He begins the story a coward, but begins to change as he figures out what truly gets you respect. On the thief scale of one to Eugenides, he's certainly no Eugenides, but he grows on you. All considered, it's easy to root for their victory over the Nirads and cruel secret agent goons.<br /><br />THE FLAME OF OLYMPUS might be inappropriate for some younger readers due to the number of deaths, at least one of which is fairly gruesome, and brief scenes of torture. It's nothing I didn't read at that age, but I try to note these things for those with sensitive children.<br /><br />Young mythology fans will enjoy THE FLAME OF OLYMPUS and eagerly wait for the rest of the series to be released stateside. And it does not fall into my series pet peeve. THE FLAME OF OLYMPUS tells a complete story, although there are threads left dangling to be addressed in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6541101481242598794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1028857274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1028857274" />
    <a title="Thenamenerd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30973062-thenamenerd"><img alt="Thenamenerd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406756516p2/30973062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028857274?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thenamenerd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thenamenerd" href="/user/show/30973062-thenamenerd">Thenamenerd</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028857274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3206996313024070232">EDIT: Review here!<br/><br/>I came into this book expecting it to be either mediocre or bad. It's somewhere in between the two.<br/><br/>This is yet another mediocre Percy Jackson cash-in series involving Roman mythology. Sorry to rain on your parade, Kate O'Hearn, but Uncle Rick beat you to it with The Heroes of Olympus series. Oh wait! This book doesn't even <em>deserve</em> to be compared to the epicness that is Heroes of Olympus.<br/><br/>Let's start with characters.<br/>Emily - Emily is our protagonist. Her main personality trait is </span>
  <span id="freeText3206996313024070232" style="display:none">EDIT: Review here!<br><br>I came into this book expecting it to be either mediocre or bad. It's somewhere in between the two.<br><br>This is yet another mediocre Percy Jackson cash-in series involving Roman mythology. Sorry to rain on your parade, Kate O'Hearn, but Uncle Rick beat you to it with The Heroes of Olympus series. Oh wait! This book doesn't even <em>deserve</em> to be compared to the epicness that is Heroes of Olympus.<br><br>Let's start with characters.<br>Emily - Emily is our protagonist. Her main personality trait is sadness about her mother's death, but that goes away after the action starts. And I'm not really sure if that's even a trait. I guess she's...determined? The point is, she's pretty bland. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I spotted the Daughter of Vesta twist near immediately, and when the reveal finally happened, they never explained anything. Is she a demigod? Was their a previous Flame of Olympus before she was born? How does this work with her mom? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Pegasus - Best character in the book. Pegasus has attitude, a sweet tooth and shows strength in battle. He's head-and-shoulders above the other Olympians when it comes to sheer coolness.<br>Joel - Why Joel even exists in this book is beyond me. I guess he's a bit more interesting than Emily, he's a bitter foster kid who is conveniently obsessed with Roman mythology. Still, Emily's reasons behind asking him to help her out are pretty lame and he doesn't add much to the story.<br>Paelen - Paelen is an Olympian thief who is one of the worst and most nonsensical characters I've ever read. He shows sympathy for others, yet does terrible things anyways and half the cast likes him for some reason and his chapters are boring as Hades. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When we thought he had died, my reaction was:<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395855940ra/9053474.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>When we found out he was alive:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405953472ra/10476492.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Emily's Dad - At least he helps a little. That's about it.<br>Diana - She has a personality...but it's annoying and overly spiteful and rude.<br>Agent J - He was mean for a little bit, then he wasn't for no reason and what. This villain confuses me.<br><br>Bad Stuff: <br>-Not explaining <em>anything</em><br>-The CRU (unrealistic government alien research team that has no rhyme or reason to it)<br>-bland characters, as said before<br>-utterly worthless gods<br>-Paelen not being dead. Oops spoiler alert! Oh wait, you shouldn't be reading this book so you shouldn't care.<br>-Agent J not believing in Olympians. And then believing in Olympians.<br>-WHY ARE THEY KEEPING STUFF SECRET FROM THE CRU IF THEY BELIEVE IN OLYMPIANS THEY COULD HELP WUT?!<br>-meh writing style<br>-Lame villain race. Oh, did I mention the baddies are the members of this species of destructible giants called the Nirads. They are lame.<br>-lots more<br><br>Good Stuff: (why it gets 2.5 stars)<br>-Pretty decent action sequences<br>-Pegasus<br>-The one book where the parents don't react badly to the magic stuff their kids keep secret. FINALLY THIS NEVER HAPPENS.<br>-Some of the bad stuff is "so-bad-it's-good"<br>-If you shut off your brain entirely, it's pretty good!<br><br>I actually enjoyed this more than I should have, which if why this book is getting 2.5 stars. The action and pacing is good and there's a few scattered good bits. Nice quick read if you're bored and want to turn off your brain. Other than that it's not worth your time. Read Percy Jackson instead. <b>2.5 STARS</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3206996313024070232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1057109357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1057109357" />
    <a title="Jessika Beaty  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6187574-jessika-beaty"><img alt="Jessika Beaty  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550024694p2/6187574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1057109357?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessika Beaty  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessika Beaty  " href="/user/show/6187574-jessika-beaty">Jessika Beaty  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1057109357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3704940798791537905">Well, I told myself I wasn't going to focus on writing reviews and become this big top reviewer. Eh. I doubt anyone reads my reviews anyway. Today world, you beautiful wonderous group of curious people for wanting to know what else is out there to read that will stimulate the mind with bubbling imagination. With a child's heart and an open mind, I invite you to open the curtains to this hidden beauty. Pegasus: the flame of Olympus. It is a tale as old as the myth itself and a wonderous re tellin</span>
  <span id="freeText3704940798791537905" style="display:none">Well, I told myself I wasn't going to focus on writing reviews and become this big top reviewer. Eh. I doubt anyone reads my reviews anyway. Today world, you beautiful wonderous group of curious people for wanting to know what else is out there to read that will stimulate the mind with bubbling imagination. With a child's heart and an open mind, I invite you to open the curtains to this hidden beauty. Pegasus: the flame of Olympus. It is a tale as old as the myth itself and a wonderous re telling of the classic rumors regarding the mythical land of Olympus and its magical inhabitants. Like many others I was browsing Barnes and nobles bookshelves and this little gem was just begging to be read. It's been ages since I've read anything and this book drew me in immediately. <br /><br />The writing style is a brilliant form of writing that relays the tone of the story to the reader. You are so drawn into the plot because she leaves you questioning what's gonna happen next. The atmosphere is dark and I am a bit skeptical on the age range. The book is deceiving its audience. Hell it left me queasy at some parts and I am 25 years old. Being an 8 year old and up read, I doubt young minds will comprehend the Gruesome nightmares of what the Nirads cause. That terror that makes you wake in the dead of night in a cold sweat, heart racing, that's what it felt like when the Nirads appeared.<br /><br /> I loved the connection between Emily and Peg. Diana was a great figure and influence to Emily and I loved the motherly role and how she cared for the girl. Paelen. He truly is magnificent as his name and character. Witty, deceitful, and caring. There are more dynamics to him then meets the eye. Joel, feisty and strong with a temper. His story was heartbreaking and the bond he and Emily formed I fell in love with. But not sure why Joel had an obsession with Pegasus to begin with. I will tell you this proceed with caution. At the government base, this one scene left me queasy. The dead soldiers. That scene was simple but you can clearly see the bloodshed and when the group arrives in Olympus I felt for Diana when she saw her brother. I cried with her. <br /><br />This book is truly a beautiful story and will certainly capture your imagination if you take the time to sit and enjoy the magic. Any young adult book needs an open mind to possibilities. I've learned that we can't always focus a review on the writing but rather the heart put into it, the way it makes you feel at the end, and with faith trust and pixie dust, just let your imagination wander. Great job to the author. Can't wait to finish the series!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3704940798791537905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1801706786" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1801706786" />
    <a title="Miki " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57180067-miki"><img alt="Miki " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587493180p2/57180067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1801706786?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miki " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miki " href="/user/show/57180067-miki">Miki </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1801706786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer158096233988693696">Alright now that I am awake and bright eyed I am going to give this book my review.<br/><br/>It was not quite meh, but I didn't quite love it either.<br/><br/>The first thing that really caught my eye was Paelen, but he wasn't really the main character of the story. It was Emily. But I'll get back to her later.<br/><br/>Paelen from the start seemed pretty cool, a little wimpy and a little self0interested, but cool and I wanted to read more about him. Instead, he spent almost the entire book in a hospital. That wasn't really </span>
  <span id="freeText158096233988693696" style="display:none">Alright now that I am awake and bright eyed I am going to give this book my review.<br /><br />It was not quite meh, but I didn't quite love it either.<br /><br />The first thing that really caught my eye was Paelen, but he wasn't really the main character of the story. It was Emily. But I'll get back to her later.<br /><br />Paelen from the start seemed pretty cool, a little wimpy and a little self0interested, but cool and I wanted to read more about him. Instead, he spent almost the entire book in a hospital. That wasn't really what I was expecting, but it wasn't really bad either since that got to show off his powers of bone manipulation. <br /><br />Now to Emily, the actual main character of the book. As soon as they mentioned the Flame I knew it was her. And not just because a friend of mine (Emily is her name actually) gave me hints a long time ago under the assumtion I would never read the book. But they just made is so <i>obvious</i>. I get it, I really do, the author was excited to make Emily the Flame. But they were shoving it down my throat. And honestly, who else would it have been? Joel? <br /><br />Nope, because they made it clear it was a girl.<br /><br />A girl who's mother would have died right?<br /><br />And who would have been connected to Pegasus?<br /><br />Who lived in New York.<br /><br />Gee, I wonder who that would be! <br /><br />Not to mention that Pegasus didn't even try to go 'looking for the Flame.' He knew what was going on!<br /><br />I didn't get any actual personality from Emily. I know its hard to give a character some personality traits, honestly I do. But there are some parts where I felt she should have conveyed a little emotion, just a little bit, and she just watched. She was okay.<br /><br />Now to Joel.<br /><br />Joel was... there.... He was a good character don't get me wrong, but he didn't seem to have any actual purpose except for knowing the myths. Even then... Why was he there again? Because he liked to draw? <br /><br />Kay yeah thanks.<br /><br />Really? I mean... really? <br /><br />You know I thought for a while that somehow Joel was connected to Pegasus too, but I was kinda disappointed when they said it was Emily. Not that Emily was bad or anything, just... What was Joel's real purpose in the story?<br /><br />He picked up Emily a few times, and actually came up with a few good plans, but other than that he was just... there. Kinda just tagging along and he got caught up in the mess.<br /><br />But Joel was cool, I liked him a lot and I guess he was there to be a friend to Emily?<br /><br />Was I the only one who didn't really get the friendship vibe off of them? Yeah I mean, <i>sure</i> in the beginning of the book they seem to be growing as friends, but then they just sort of exsist among each other for the rest of the chapters but by the end they're like best friends.<br /><br />Kay cool.<br /><br />Diana now...<br /><br />I won't even try to downplay this; Diana was awesome. She was a strong female character with actual emotions who knew how to take charge when she needed to and was an awesome fighter. Diana ruled!<br /><br />I didn't really like how fragile the she was at some points. She's an Olympian for crying out loud!<br /><br />I know I know the Flame went out and she was still pretty powerful and all, but still.<br /><br />At least they didn't try and play her as a damsel in distress. Otherwise I would have lost my crap talking about her.<br /><br />Steve... He was meh. There kinda and then not there either. That's all.<br /><br />Pegasus.... He was cool?<br /><br />I honestly don't know how I feel about Pegasus. I don't dislike him, and I'm not sure if I love him.<br /><br />The entire book to me kinda seemed... lacking detail.<br /><br />That's what I've been meaning to say this entire time! Lacking detail!<br /><br />I'm not going to pretend to be some super awesome writer who knows everything, that's stupid, but I felt like as soon as I read the words coming off the page I forgot them. And it wasn't for a lack of trying to get into the story either. I read it will two o'clock in the morning, but it was very forgettable. <br /><br /><br /><br />Overall, it wasn't bad. There was a ton of nice aspects in the story that I enjoyed. I pointed out some negative and not much postive, but the postive has been used a million times by now.<br /><br />This is just my opnion honestly, so don't eat me if I don't adore the book with all my heart and soul. Sorry, it just wasn't really up my alley. And there isn't much I could do to change that.<br /><br />This seems like the kind of book that in a week I'll be annoyed with. But I will still read the others if I can ever find them.<br /><br />And with that *waves* allll done!</span>
  <a data-text-id="158096233988693696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_331920949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331920949" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4862284-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464472130p2/4862284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331920949?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/4862284-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442444096" href="/book/show/12541481-the-flame-of-olympus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331920949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5307107981137994642">Pegasus: The Flame of Olympus was such an enjoyable book. It honestly felt more like a middle grade than a young adult, even though every label I could find listed it as young adult. I love Greek/Roman mythology so even from the Prologue I was hooked. Kate did a very good job at taking mythology and putting a very interesting twist on it.<br/><br/>I'm sure most of you know at least some Greek/Roman mythology. This book includes a lot of characters from mythology such as Jupiter, Pegasus, Neptune, Hercules</span>
  <span id="freeText5307107981137994642" style="display:none">Pegasus: The Flame of Olympus was such an enjoyable book. It honestly felt more like a middle grade than a young adult, even though every label I could find listed it as young adult. I love Greek/Roman mythology so even from the Prologue I was hooked. Kate did a very good job at taking mythology and putting a very interesting twist on it.<br /><br />I'm sure most of you know at least some Greek/Roman mythology. This book includes a lot of characters from mythology such as Jupiter, Pegasus, Neptune, Hercules and more. Granted a lot of them are only mentioned once or twice throughout the book it was still really cool to have them all in it. Kate did a fantastic job making the battle between the Olympians and the Nirads feel really epic. And seeing how Emily and Joel get caught up in the story is also pretty exciting. The battle is pretty much the meat of this story, between the battle and trying to protect the flame of Olympus to keep both worlds safe.<br /><br />Emily and Joel get caught up in all of this after a major storm hits New York. The storm is pretty much what sets the story in motion with the introduction of Pegasus and Paelen. Even though Pegasus is a horse, he is still such a great part of the story. Kate was able to create an awesome background for Pegasus and it really felt like he was more than just a horse. Paelen is a really great character to, being a thief he is somewhat hard to like but he does have some good qualities. All in all it's just a really great group of characters, Kate really did a good job writing them to where they all flow together nicely.<br /><br />I'm really excited to see where this series goes, and what becomes of all of the characters after what happened at the end. I was really impressed by the ending though, I will admit I was expecting it to be a happy and perfect ending at first just because of how the book felt but it ended up being a really great ending which has somewhat of a mix of good and bad. I didn't really feel like it ended on some huge cliffhanger either which was nice, it just got me excited to read the next book to find out what happens next.<br /><br />If you like Greek/Roman mythology or are just looking for a exciting and fast paced book to read this summer I would highly suggest picking this one up. It's fairly light, I found it to be a really fast read once I was actually able to sit down for an extended period of time to read it. So I feel like it's once of those books that can easily be read in a day, and have it be a really fun experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5307107981137994642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442444096" href="/book/show/12541481-the-flame-of-olympus">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4964628-angie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805509264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8462142802847056371"><b>Synopsis:</b> <i>"A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.<br/><br/>When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during a terrible storm, Emily's life changes forever. Suddenly allied with a winged horse she'd always thought was mythical, Emily is thrust into the center of a fierce battle between the Roman gods and a terrifying race of multiarmed stone warriors called the Nirads. Emily must team up with a thief named Paelen, the goddess D</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8462142802847056371" style="display:none"><b>Synopsis:</b> <i>"A young girl, a winged horse, and a war of epic proportions make for an adventurous start to an exciting new trilogy.<br /><br />When Pegasus crashes onto a Manhattan roof during a terrible storm, Emily's life changes forever. Suddenly allied with a winged horse she'd always thought was mythical, Emily is thrust into the center of a fierce battle between the Roman gods and a terrifying race of multiarmed stone warriors called the Nirads. Emily must team up with a thief named Paelen, the goddess Diana, and a boy named Joel in order to return Pegasus to Olympus and rescue the gods from a certain death.<br /><br />Along the way, Emily and her companions will fight monsters, run from a government agency that is prepared to dissect Pegasus, and even fly above the Manhattan skyline-all as part of a quest to save Olympus before time runs out."</i><br /><br /><b>My Review:</b> While I was having trouble settling into a book, I picked this one up off my TBR shelf and it hit the spot. I could not stop reading it! I loved the fantasy, myths, and adventure all wrapped into modern day New York City. The characters developed beautifully and I ended up falling in love with them. I really enjoyed how Pegasus became such a big character himself. The story line felt so new and refreshing. It would be fun for young adult guys and girls to read, there is plenty of adventure and fantasy for all. I loved this so much that the morning after finishing it I went out and purchased the next book in the trilogy (and happened to see the third just came out but couldn't get it this time).</span>

<div id="review_2281116181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281116181" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59362347-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281116181?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/59362347-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281116181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3080484535831442524">The Flame Of Olympus<br/>The book is called Pegasus, Flame of Olympus, by Kate O’hearn. It’s a crossover story between Emily Jacobs and a god named Paelen.<br/>It starts with Emily sitting by the window watching the biggest thunderstorm that had ever happened in New york city. Emily’s dad Steve Jacobs is a cop and is working. While Olympus is having a battle between the Nirads and the roman gods. The flame of Olympus has been dimming, and the gods are weakened by the that, without the flame the gods do no</span>
  <span id="freeText3080484535831442524" style="display:none">The Flame Of Olympus<br />The book is called Pegasus, Flame of Olympus, by Kate O’hearn. It’s a crossover story between Emily Jacobs and a god named Paelen.<br />It starts with Emily sitting by the window watching the biggest thunderstorm that had ever happened in New york city. Emily’s dad Steve Jacobs is a cop and is working. While Olympus is having a battle between the Nirads and the roman gods. The flame of Olympus has been dimming, and the gods are weakened by the that, without the flame the gods do not have enough power to defeat the Nirads. While the battle rages on Paelen, a thief, wants to take Pegasus for himself and escape the battle. During the battle Jupiter sends Pegasus to find the girl who holds the flame of Olympus inside her. But when Pegasus arrives at Earth Paelen follows him using Mercury's winged sandals. Lighting strikes them both, and Pegasus lands on Emily’s roof. While Paelen disappears. Emily might need help from Joel to figure this out.<br /><br />This book was definitely worth my time to read, it felt like I was there feeling what they were feeling. I didn’t find any part of the book slow. There was a lot of action in it and some sad moments. This book had all kind of emotion in it. Fear, curiosity, happiness, sadness and anger. I didn’t really like the part where they get captured, or when Emily got hurt. But it was kinda worth it to make the book exciting. I liked the way that the author made the gods roman, I found that interesting I’m more used to them being greek. It was a new experience for me. I liked it a lot. I remember being scared of a big thunderstorm like Emily. But no Pegasus crashed on my roof. Emily has a very determined personality, she would do anything for her friends. Paelen’s personality at first was the opposite of Emily's. Throughout the book Paelen became friends with Emily and Joel, he learned what it’s like to be, and to have a friend who treats him more than a thief. This book made me feel all kinds of emotion, scared, happy, sad and a little bit of anger. But I loved it anyway.<br /><br />I think the theme of this book is that we should trust our friends and don’t judge someone who we never met. Like when Emily had to trust Joel to keep Pegasus a secret, and when they both thought that Paelen was just a thief and cared about no one but himself. But he proved them wrong by helping them escape the police. Think book is definitely one that I would read again. I really liked all of it even the parts I didn’t like, I loved them.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3080484535831442524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4179916064739902772" style="display:none">I was really in the mood for some middle grade fantasy book and I picked this one solely for the cover.<br />I have pretty much nothing nice to say about this story.<br />Almost everything is conveniently left unexplained but the plot somehow moves forward. The characters and their communication is as deep as a puddle after a 5 minute rain. That is, they are too juvenile despite them being 13 years old and also the plot has some darker elements like torture and they are in almost every way contrary to undeveloped general storyline.<br />And one of my biggest pet peeves is the miserably inadequate role of the Olympian Gods. They are so weak and pitiable which is really disturbing to read about and all but pisses me off.<br />The mental image in my head featuring majestic Pegasus and it's important role in this book couldn't save it in the end. The plot as a whole, the characters, the dialogues and almost everything else is just weak even for a children's book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_395258297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/395258297" />
    <a title="Kaitlin Hillerich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5689264-kaitlin-hillerich"><img alt="Kaitlin Hillerich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331675309p2/5689264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/395258297?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin Hillerich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin Hillerich" href="/user/show/5689264-kaitlin-hillerich">Kaitlin Hillerich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5689264-kaitlin-hillerich?shelf=books-read-in-2012">books-read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer395258297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4967781539062128817"><br/>Read more of my reviews on my <a href='http://ireadwritelove.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a><br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/><br/> <i>"It's really you isn't it?" Emily whispered softly as she stroked the soft muzzle. "You're Pegasus, aren't you?"<br/> The stallion...nudged her hand, inviting another stroke. In that one rain-drenched instant, Emily felt her world changing. Forever. (p. 33)</i><br/><br/>One stormy night Pegasus crashes onto the roof of Emily's apartment in New York City. She soon learns that there is a war going on in Olympus and that the gods are being overthrown by the vicious, monstro</span>
  <span id="freeText4967781539062128817" style="display:none"><br />Read more of my reviews on my <a href="http://ireadwritelove.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br /><br /> <i>"It's really you isn't it?" Emily whispered softly as she stroked the soft muzzle. "You're Pegasus, aren't you?"<br /> The stallion...nudged her hand, inviting another stroke. In that one rain-drenched instant, Emily felt her world changing. Forever. (p. 33)</i><br /><br />One stormy night Pegasus crashes onto the roof of Emily's apartment in New York City. She soon learns that there is a war going on in Olympus and that the gods are being overthrown by the vicious, monstrous Nirads. These creatures have followed Pegasus to earth, along with a thief named Paelen who is after the stallion's golden bridle.<br /><br />Emily must work together with a boy named Joel and the goddess Diana to return Pegasus to Olympus and defeat the Nirads before it is too late and both of their worlds are destroyed.<br /><br /><br /><b>Our Heroine: Emily</b><br /><br /> <i>"No!" Emily cried. "This is impossible!"<br /> More lightning lit the rooftop, confirming what Emily was trying so hard to deny.<br /> A white horse with golden hooves and vast white wings was lying on its side in the middle of her mother's rose garden. (p. 29)</i><br /><br /> Emily was a sweet, caring girl and the relationship between her and Pegasus was really cute. My favorite part was when she brought him carrots and apples and a tub of ice cream for herself, and Pegasus ended up eating the ice cream. It was also sweet how protective Pegasus was of Emily.<br /><br />However, while Emily did have likeable and sympathetic qualities (she is mourning the death of her mother), her character wasn't very developed. I also didn't feel like her character had changed at the end of the story as a result of her adventure. <br /><br /><br /><b>Our Villain: The Nirads</b><br /><br /> <i>"Emily could see that the Nirad's eyes were jet-black with no whites or color at all. Its teeth were large, sharp points, and it was drooling as it made ferocious, guttural sounds...it flexed its four arms, which ended in filthy hands and fingers with long, sharp claws." (p. 132)</i><br /><br />The Nirads are the main villains of the story. They are four-armed monster warriors that appear to be indestructible and in the beginning of the story they have taken over Olympus.<br /><br />They weren't really the best villains honestly. It's never explained where they came from, or what exactly they were after. With no motive, it felt like they were there just for the sake of the story having a villain.<br /><br />Another villain of the story is a secret government agency called CRU, which researches strange phenomenon such as aliens and UFO's. They end up capturing one of the Olympians who accidentally came to earth with Pegasus early on, which leads to a series of interrogation scenes.<br /><br />Basically the same questions and answers are repeated over and over and over to the point where it gets really annoying to read. The agents believe in aliens but refuse to accept that the Olympians could be real despite all the obvious evidence that continues to pile up (a winged horse, winged sandals, the toga).<br /><br />I mean come on how thick could you be??<br /><br /><br /><b>Main Characters</b><br /><br /> Paelen<br /><br /> <i>"But Paelen had no intention of fighting. He wasn't a warrior. He was a thief with plans of his own, which didn't include getting killed in a battle they couldn't possibly win." (p. 2)</i><br /><br />Paelen was probably one of the most interesting characters. He's a cowardly, selfish thief who accidentally follows Pegasus to earth. He wants to steal Pegasus's bridle for himself so he can control the stallion and leave Olympus because he feels like he doesn't belong.<br /><br />He also has a talent for being able to escape any prison, because he can stretch his bones. I felt like Paelen was one of the character's who had more depth and who developed the most throughout the story.<br /><br /> Joel<br /><br /> <i>"Finally someone came to mind. Someone from her school who would be strong enough to pull out the spear. Someone who was always sketching pictures of winged horses in his textbooks. The trouble was, he was the meanest boy in Emily's class. He was probably the meanest boy in the whole school." (p. 55)</i><br /><br />Joel is an angry, troubled foster kid who Emily knows from school. I found it a bit unbelievable that she would go to him for help with Pegasus since she didn't know him at all he wasn't a very friendly person.<br /><br />Joel had a bit more depth than most of the characters, and he also developed some throughout the story. He and Emily become friends, and the friendship between them was sweet.<br /><br /><br /><b>To Read Or Not To Read? </b><br /><br /> The initial idea of this book is very intriguing, but in all honesty the writing needed a lot of work. The dialogue especially was very weak and awkward (and often cheesy), and a lot of times characters would state things to each other that they already knew solely for the reader's benefit. There was also lots of repetition of the same information.<br /><br />I still enjoyed the story itself despite this, though it would have been much better had the writing been polished up. It was a fun, heartwarming, light read and I think that younger kids would really enjoy it.<br /><br />I think though, with a younger audience in mind that this book should have been shorter because 400 pages can be daunting for younger readers, even if it is larger text that reads quickly.<br /><br />All in all, a cute story!<br /><br /><br />Writing: 2/5<br />Characters: 2/5<br />Plot: 3/5<br />Creativity/Originality: 4/5<br />Kept me interested: 4/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="4967781539062128817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer526450318360258729">When Pegasus crashes onto Emily's apartment rooftop, she quickly befriends both it and the bully from her class, Joel, forming a bond as the city falls to a blackout. When monsters begin invading New York City, however, she must brave Olympic dangers to save the lives of her friends - and her home. O'Hearn begins an entertaining series with this exciting novel that will please fans of myth and legend. Emily takes to the streets as she and her allies try to restore the treasured Flame of the gods</span>
  <span id="freeText526450318360258729" style="display:none">When Pegasus crashes onto Emily's apartment rooftop, she quickly befriends both it and the bully from her class, Joel, forming a bond as the city falls to a blackout. When monsters begin invading New York City, however, she must brave Olympic dangers to save the lives of her friends - and her home. O'Hearn begins an entertaining series with this exciting novel that will please fans of myth and legend. Emily takes to the streets as she and her allies try to restore the treasured Flame of the gods...even if the cost ends up being more than they can bear.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X2jSbzslQTXLy57M2wYnBAH2AocPWYBz12ds97PNcrePuLodom9s7n7tP9UcZIWEKf2VuAouaAMG52X+rIJw+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Pi6YaHv/i49M+TuvMiwsLPqQtkg7jdG8zNz5nfIPC/ru/vAa4rWmVPnfmrb1To6s0pshdz76OcwdXPCU7UAJtQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4768632054352599957">Kate O'Hearn was born in Toronto Canada, but raised in the heart of New York City and has lived in many places throughout her life. These days, she calls the south coast of England home. She has 3 brothers, no sisters and is passionate about animals and their causes and has many animal friends. (Pets)<br/><br/>Over the course of her life she has had several careers before finding her real love, writing chil</span>
  <span id="freeText4768632054352599957" style="display:none">Kate O'Hearn was born in Toronto Canada, but raised in the heart of New York City and has lived in many places throughout her life. These days, she calls the south coast of England home. She has 3 brothers, no sisters and is passionate about animals and their causes and has many animal friends. (Pets)<br /><br />Over the course of her life she has had several careers before finding her real love, writing children's books. Being the only girl in family of boys, she grew up a true tom-boy and always loved books with high adventure. But one of the problems she discovered was a lack of female leads in these adventure books.<br /><br />When she started to write, Kate decided to address this imbalance and now writes high fantasy adventures with strong, compassionate and adventure loving girl heroes. There are plenty of boys in the story to keep it interesting and challenging, but she believes that a girl hero can be as brave, strong and adventurous as a boy.<br /><br />She insists that adventures are for everyone!<br /><br />So come and enjoy a few adventures with her...</span>
